> The spawner will just copy it to each client root and it will “know” the structure.
> 
> Changes vs last version:
> 
> - Uses the **new top-levels** (`10_profile`, `20_engagement`, etc.).  
> - Adds `build_index` to create a **static JSON index** from docs under `60_kb/kb_vault` and `50_work`.  
> - Index is written to `portal/data/docs_index.json` for the portal RAG agent.
> 
> ```python
> #!/usr/bin/env python3
> """
> QiAlly Client Agent (flat, portable)
> 
> Commands:
>   validate   : check structure, depth, large files
>   compact    : move large files to archive and leave pointers
>   report     : generate simple HTML health report
>   build_index: build lightweight JSON index for the portal RAG search
> 
> Usage:
>   python client_agent.py validate
>   python client_agent.py compact
>   python client_agent.py report
>   python client_agent.py build_index
> """
> 
> import sys
> import json
> import shutil
> from pathlib import Path
> from datetime import datetime
> 
> ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parent
> META_PATH = ROOT / "client.meta.json"
> 
> REQUIRED_TOP_LEVEL = [
>     "_system",
>     "10_profile",
>     "20_engagement",
>     "30_ops",
>     "40_finance",
>     "50_work",
>     "60_kb",
>     "70_archive",
>     "kb_site",
>     "portal",
> ]
> 
> LARGE_FILE_MB = 25
> MAX_DEPTH = 4
> 
> 
> def load_meta() -> dict:
>     if META_PATH.exists():
>         try:
>             return json.loads(META_PATH.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))
>         except Exception:
>             pass
>     return {}
> 
> 
> def validate() -> int:
>     print("=== VALIDATE ===")
>     meta = load_meta()
>     if meta:
>         print(f"Client: {meta.get('client_name', 'Unknown')} ({meta.get('client_code', 'c.unknown')})")
>         print(f"QID   : {meta.get('qid', 'N/A')}")
>     else:
>         print("WARN: client.meta.json missing or unreadable.")
> 
>     print("\n[1] Top-level folders")
>     missing = []
>     for name in REQUIRED_TOP_LEVEL:
>         p = ROOT / name
>         if not p.exists():
>             missing.append(name)
>             print(f"  - MISSING : {name}")
>         else:
>             print(f"  - OK      : {name}")
> 
>     print("\n[2] Orphan files at root")
>     ignored = {"client.meta.json", "README.md", "client_agent.py"}
>     orphans = []
>     for item in ROOT.iterdir():
>         if item.is_file() and item.name not in ignored:
>             orphans.append(item.name)
>             print(f"  - ORPHAN FILE: {item.name}")
> 
>     print("\n[3] Depth check (>{} levels)".format(MAX_DEPTH))
>     too_deep = []
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if path.is_dir():
>             continue
>         rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>         depth = len(rel.parts)
>         if depth > MAX_DEPTH:
>             too_deep.append(str(rel))
> 
>     if too_deep:
>         print(f"Found {len(too_deep)} items deeper than {MAX_DEPTH} levels:")
>         for rel in too_deep[:20]:
>             print(f"  - {rel}")
>         if len(too_deep) > 20:
>             print(f"  ... +{len(too_deep) - 20} more")
>     else:
>         print("No paths beyond depth limit.")
> 
>     print("\n[4] Large files (>{} MB)".format(LARGE_FILE_MB))
>     large = []
>     threshold = LARGE_FILE_MB * 1024 * 1024
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if path.is_file():
>             try:
>                 size = path.stat().st_size
>             except OSError:
>                 continue
>             if size >= threshold:
>                 large.append((path, size))
> 
>     if large:
>         for path, size in sorted(large, key=lambda x: x[1], reverse=True):
>             rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>             mb = size / (1024 * 1024)
>             print(f"  - {rel} ({mb:.1f} MB)")
>     else:
>         print("No large files found.")
> 
>     print("\n[✓] Validation complete.\n")
>     return 0
> 
> 
> def compact() -> int:
>     print("=== COMPACT ===")
>     archive_root = ROOT / "70_archive"
>     archive_root.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
> 
>     large_assets_dir = archive_root / "large_assets"
>     large_assets_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
> 
>     threshold = LARGE_FILE_MB * 1024 * 1024
>     moved = 0
> 
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if not path.is_file():
>             continue
>         if path.is_relative_to(archive_root):
>             continue
>         if path.name in {"client.meta.json", "client_agent.py"}:
>             continue
> 
>         try:
>             size = path.stat().st_size
>         except OSError:
>             continue
> 
>         if size >= threshold:
>             rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>             target = large_assets_dir / rel
>             target.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>             print(f"  - Moving large file to archive: {rel}")
>             shutil.move(str(path), str(target))
>             moved += 1
> 
>             pointer_path = ROOT / rel
>             pointer_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>             pointer_path.write_text(
>                 f"This file was moved to archive:\n"
>                 f"  70_archive/large_assets/{rel}\n"
>                 f"Size: {size / (1024*1024):.1f} MB\n",
>                 encoding="utf-8",
>             )
> 
>     print(f"\n[✓] Compact complete. Large files moved: {moved}\n")
>     return 0
> 
> 
> def report() -> int:
>     print("=== REPORT ===")
>     meta = load_meta()
>     now = datetime.utcnow().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S UTC")
>     summary = {
>         "generated_at": now,
>         "client": {
>             "name": meta.get("client_name", "Unknown"),
>             "code": meta.get("client_code", "c.unknown"),
>             "qid": meta.get("qid", "N/A"),
>         },
>         "folders": {},
>         "largest_files": [],
>     }
> 
>     for top in ROOT.iterdir():
>         if not top.is_dir():
>             continue
>         size = 0
>         count = 0
>         for path in top.rglob("*"):
>             if path.is_file():
>                 try:
>                     size += path.stat().st_size
>                     count += 1
>                 except OSError:
>                     continue
>         summary["folders"][top.name] = {
>             "files": count,
>             "size_bytes": size,
>         }
> 
>     all_files = []
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if path.is_file():
>             try:
>                 size = path.stat().st_size
>             except OSError:
>                 continue
>             all_files.append((path, size))
> 
>     top_n = sorted(all_files, key=lambda x: x[1], reverse=True)[:20]
>     for path, size in top_n:
>         rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>         summary["largest_files"].append(
>             {"path": str(rel), "size_bytes": size}
>         )
> 
>     reports_dir = ROOT / "70_archive" / "reports"
>     reports_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>     ts = datetime.utcnow().strftime("%Y%m%d_%H%M%S")
>     html_path = reports_dir / f"health_{ts}.html"
> 
>     def fmt_size(b: int) -> str:
>         mb = b / (1024 * 1024)
>         return f"{mb:.1f} MB"
> 
>     lines = []
>     lines.append("<!DOCTYPE html>")
>     lines.append("<html><head><meta charset='utf-8'><title>Client Health Report</title>")
>     lines.append("<style>body{font-family:sans-serif;max-width:900px;margin:2rem auto;} table{border-collapse:collapse;width:100%;} th,td{border:1px solid #ccc;padding:4px 8px;text-align:left;} h1,h2{margin-top:1.5rem;}</style>")
>     lines.append("</head><body>")
>     lines.append("<h1>Client Health Report</h1>")
>     lines.append(f"<p>Generated: {now}</p>")
>     lines.append(f"<p>Client: {summary['client']['name']} ({summary['client']['code']}) – QID: {summary['client']['qid']}</p>")
> 
>     lines.append("<h2>Folder Summary</h2>")
>     lines.append("<table><tr><th>Folder</th><th>Files</th><th>Size</th></tr>")
>     for name, info in sorted(summary["folders"].items()):
>         lines.append(f"<tr><td>{name}</td><td>{info['files']}</td><td>{fmt_size(info['size_bytes'])}</td></tr>")
>     lines.append("</table>")
> 
>     lines.append("<h2>Largest Files</h2>")
>     if summary["largest_files"]:
>         lines.append("<table><tr><th>Path</th><th>Size</th></tr>")
>         for item in summary["largest_files"]:
>             lines.append(f"<tr><td>{item['path']}</td><td>{fmt_size(item['size_bytes'])}</td></tr>")
>         lines.append("</table>")
>     else:
>         lines.append("<p>No files found.</p>")
> 
>     lines.append("</body></html>")
>     html_path.write_text("\n".join(lines), encoding="utf-8")
> 
>     print(f"[✓] Report written to: {html_path}")
>     return 0
> 
> 
> # --------- RAG index builder (for portal) ---------
> 
> def extract_text(path: Path) -> str:
>     """
>     Ultra-simple extraction:
>     - .md/.txt: return raw text
>     - .html/.htm: strip tags in a naive way
>     Everything else: return empty.
>     """
>     try:
>         text = path.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")
>     except Exception:
>         return ""
> 
>     if path.suffix.lower() in {".md", ".txt"}:
>         return text
> 
>     if path.suffix.lower() in {".html", ".htm"}:
>         # naive tag stripper
>         import re
>         return re.sub(r"<[^>]+>", " ", text)
> 
>     return ""
> 
> 
> def build_index() -> int:
>     """
>     Build a light JSON index for the portal RAG agent.
> 
>     Looks at:
>       - 60_kb/kb_vault
>       - 50_work
> 
>     Writes:
>       - portal/data/docs_index.json
>     """
>     print("=== BUILD INDEX ===")
>     kb_root = ROOT / "60_kb" / "kb_vault"
>     work_root = ROOT / "50_work"
>     docs = []
> 
>     for base in [kb_root, work_root]:
>         if not base.exists():
>             continue
>         for path in base.rglob("*"):
>             if not path.is_file():
>                 continue
>             if path.suffix.lower() not in {".md", ".txt", ".html", ".htm"}:
>                 continue
> 
>             rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>             text = extract_text(path)
>             if not text.strip():
>                 continue
> 
>             # keep first chunk as summary-ish
>             snippet = " ".join(text.split()[:80])
> 
>             docs.append({
>                 "id": str(rel),
>                 "title": path.stem,
>                 "path": str(rel),
>                 "snippet": snippet,
>                 "content": text,
>             })
> 
>     portal_data = ROOT / "portal" / "data"
>     portal_data.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>     index_path = portal_data / "docs_index.json"
>     index_path.write_text(json.dumps(docs, indent=2), encoding="utf-8")
> 
>     print(f"[✓] Indexed {len(docs)} docs into {index_path}")
>     return 0
> 
> 
> def main(argv: list[str]) -> int:
>     if len(argv) < 2:
>         print("Usage: python client_agent.py [validate|compact|report|build_index]")
>         return 1
> 
>     cmd = argv[1].lower()
>     if cmd == "validate":
>         return validate()
>     if cmd == "compact":
>         return compact()
>     if cmd == "report":
>         return report()
>     if cmd == "build_index":
>         return build_index()
> 
>     print(f"Unknown command: {cmd}")
>     return 1
> 
> 
> if __name__ == "__main__":
>     raise SystemExit(main(sys.argv))
> ```
> 
> That’s your **flat, self-contained “maintenance + index” agent**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Portal RAG agent (HTML5 + JS only)
> 
> The index is built by `build_index()` into:
> 
> `portal/data/docs_index.json`
> 
> Now the portal only needs:
> 
> - `portal/index.html`  
> - `portal/js/search.js`  
> 
> ### `portal/index.html`
> 
> Very simple shell:
> 
> ```html
> <!DOCTYPE html>
> <html lang="en">
> <head>
>   <meta charset="UTF-8" />
>   <title>Client Portal</title>
>   <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1" />
>   <style>
>     body { font-family: system-ui, -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, sans-serif; margin: 1.5rem; max-width: 960px; }
>     input[type="search"] { width: 100%; padding: 0.5rem; margin-bottom: 1rem; box-sizing: border-box; }
>     .result { border-bottom: 1px solid #ddd; padding: 0.5rem 0; }
>     .result h3 { margin: 0 0 0.25rem 0; font-size: 1rem; }
>     .result small { color: #666; }
>     .result p { margin: 0.25rem 0 0.5rem 0; font-size: 0.9rem; }
>   </style>
> </head>
> <body>
>   <h1>Client Portal</h1>
> 
>   <section>
>     <h2>Search Knowledge</h2>
>     <input id="searchInput" type="search" placeholder="Search docs..." autocomplete="off" />
>     <div id="results"></div>
>   </section>
> 
>   <section>
>     <h2>Shortcuts</h2>
>     <ul>
>       <li><a href="../kb_site/index.html" target="_blank">Open KB Site</a></li>
>       <li><a href="../60_kb/kb_vault" target="_blank">Browse KB Vault</a></li>
>       <li><a href="../70_archive/reports" target="_blank">Health Reports</a></li>
>     </ul>
>   </section>
> 
>   <script src="js/search.js"></script>
> </body>
> </html>
> ```
> 
> ### `portal/js/search.js`
> 
> Naive, but effective: loads `docs_index.json`, does simple token scoring, shows top matches. No frameworks, no build.
> 
> ```javascript
> (function() {
>   const input = document.getElementById("searchInput");
>   const resultsEl = document.getElementById("results");
>   let docs = [];
> 
>   async function loadIndex() {
>     try {
>       const res = await fetch("data/docs_index.json", { cache: "no-store" });
>       if (!res.ok) throw new Error("Failed to load index");
>       docs = await res.json();
>       console.log("Loaded docs index:", docs.length, "docs");
>     } catch (err) {
>       console.error(err);
>       resultsEl.innerHTML = "<p><em>Could not load search index. Run client_agent.py build_index.</em></p>";
>     }
>   }
> 
>   function scoreDoc(doc, terms) {
>     const text = (doc.content || "").toLowerCase();
>     let score = 0;
>     for (const t of terms) {
>       if (!t) continue;
>       const occurrences = text.split(t).length - 1;
>       score += occurrences;
>     }
>     return score;
>   }
> 
>   function renderResults(matches) {
>     if (!matches.length) {
>       resultsEl.innerHTML = "<p><em>No matches.</em></p>";
>       return;
>     }
>     const fragment = document.createDocumentFragment();
>     matches.slice(0, 25).forEach(doc => {
>       const div = document.createElement("div");
>       div.className = "result";
> 
>       const h3 = document.createElement("h3");
>       h3.textContent = doc.title || doc.path;
>       div.appendChild(h3);
> 
>       const small = document.createElement("small");
>       small.textContent = doc.path;
>       div.appendChild(small);
> 
>       const p = document.createElement("p");
>       p.textContent = doc.snippet || "";
>       div.appendChild(p);
> 
>       const link = document.createElement("a");
>       link.href = "../" + doc.path;
>       link.textContent = "Open";
>       link.target = "_blank";
>       div.appendChild(link);
> 
>       fragment.appendChild(div);
>     });
>     resultsEl.innerHTML = "";
>     resultsEl.appendChild(fragment);
>   }
> 
>   function onSearch() {
>     const query = input.value.trim().toLowerCase();
>     if (!query) {
>       resultsEl.innerHTML = "";
>       return;
>     }
>     const terms = query.split(/\s+/).filter(Boolean);
>     const scored = docs
>       .map(d => ({ doc: d, score: scoreDoc(d, terms) }))
>       .filter(x => x.score > 0)
>       .sort((a, b) => b.score - a.score);
>     renderResults(scored.map(x => x.doc));
>   }
> 
>   input.addEventListener("input", () => {
>     // small debounce
>     if (input._timer) clearTimeout(input._timer);
>     input._timer = setTimeout(onSearch, 150);
>   });
> 
>   loadIndex();
> })();
> ```
> 
> That’s your **“portal RAG agent”**:
> 
> - Offline.  
> - No backend.  
> - Uses the JSON index from `client_agent.py`.  
> - HTML+JS only, so it survives anywhere (local file, static hosting, CF Pages, etc.).
> 
> ---
> 
> ## What you should change in the template repo
> 
> 1. Update `CLIENT_MANIFEST` in `client_spawner.py` to the **flat** version above.  
> 2. Put `client_agent.py` into `templates/client_agent/client_agent.py`.  
> 3. Update `TEMPLATE_MAPPINGS` in `client_spawner.py` to include:
> 
> ```python
> TEMPLATE_MAPPINGS = {
>     "kb_site": "kb_site",
>     "portal_shell": "portal",
>     "system_templates": "_system/templates",
>     "kb_vault_seed": "60_kb/kb_vault",
>     "client_agent": ".",  # drops client_agent.py in client root
> }
> ```
> 
> 4. In `templates/portal_shell/`, add:
>    - `index.html` as above.
>    - `js/search.js` as above.
>    - `data/` (empty folder, will be filled by `build_index`).
> 
> Then the flow for a brand-new client is:
> 
> ```bash
> # from qi-client-template/
> ./start.sh     # choose "New client"
> 
> # in the new client repo:
> python client_agent.py validate
> python client_agent.py build_index
> python client_agent.py report
> ```
> 
> Open `portal/index.html` in a browser → you’ve got search over their docs with zero extra infrastructure.
> 
> If you want, next step we tighten `PATTERN_RULES` around the new manifest (so invoices go to `40_finance/invoices`, etc.), but the core skeleton is now consistent with your “flat, light, HTML5” rule.

### User
> tight pattern rules lets try to think of everything, auto file renaming and moving, and did you get mini gina in the template to be the chat bot for the client repo, we can use a very small nano llm no to keep it all portal and offline but still useful?

### Assistant
> Alright, let’s level this up without turning it into Kubernetes-in-a-folder.
> 
> We’ll do three things:
> 
> 1. **Tight pattern rules + auto renaming/moving** (in `client_agent.py`)  
> 2. **An `organize` command** that runs those rules automatically  
> 3. **“Mini Gina”**: a tiny portal chat that does RAG over docs_index, with an optional hook to a local nano-LLM if you want
> 
> I’ll give you code you can drop into the **template repo**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1. Tight pattern rules for the flat manifest
> 
> We’re aligning to this structure:
> 
> ```text
> <client_root>/
> ├── _system/
> ├── 10_profile/
> ├── 20_engagement/
> ├── 30_ops/
> ├── 40_finance/
> ├── 50_work/
> ├── 60_kb/
> ├── 70_archive/
> ├── kb_site/
> └── portal/
> ```
> 
> ### Pattern rules (conceptual)
> 
> We’ll classify based on filename (lowercased) and extension:
> 
> - **Profile / IDs**
>   - Keywords: `id`, `passport`, `license`, `ssn`, `dob`, `profile`, `resume`, `cv`
>   - → `10_profile/ids` or `10_profile/personal`
> - **Engagement**
>   - `proposal`, `quote`, `scope`, `msa`, `sow`, `agreement`, `contract`, `nda`, `policy`, `terms`
>   - → `20_engagement/proposals` or `20_engagement/contracts` or `20_engagement/policies`
> - **Ops**
>   - `onboarding`, `checklist`, `sop`, `procedure`, `playbook`, `access`, `password`, `login`, `howto`
>   - → `30_ops/onboarding`, `30_ops/checklists`, `30_ops/sops`, `30_ops/access`
> - **Finance**
>   - `invoice`, `inv_`, `bill`, `statement`, `bank`, `deposit`, `payout`, `refund`, `receipt`, `expense`, `tax`, `1040`, `w2`, `1099`
>   - → `40_finance/invoices`, `40_finance/expenses`, `40_finance/bank`, `40_finance/tax`, `40_finance/reports`
> - **Work (case/project stuff)**
>   - Immigration-ish: `i-589`, `i589`, `i-360`, `i360`, `i-130`, `i130`, `ds-260`, `ds260`, `uscis`, `rfe`, `affidavit`
>     - → `50_work/immigration`
>   - Marketing-ish: `campaign`, `adset`, `creative`, `landing`, `funnel`, `brief`
>     - → `50_work/marketing`
>   - Generic: `project`, `deliverable`, `timeline`, `plan`, `strategy`, `spec`
>     - → `50_work/projects`
> - **KB / References**
>   - `notes`, `meeting`, `summary`, `faq`, `guide`, `manual`, `how-to`, `reference`
>   - → `60_kb/kb_vault` or `60_kb/references`
> - **Media**
>   - Extensions: `.png`, `.jpg`, `.jpeg`, `.gif`, `.heic`, `.mp4`, `.mov`, `.m4a`, `.mp3`, `.wav`
>   - → `60_kb/media`
> - **Legal general**
>   - `complaint`, `lawsuit`, `subpoena`, `summons`, `court`, `case_no`, `case-`
>   - → `60_kb/legal`
> - **Fallback**
>   - Anything else not already in the correct top-level goes to `60_kb/references`.
> 
> We’ll encode that as `PATTERN_RULES` and use it in an `organize` command.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. Updated `client_agent.py` with `organize` command
> 
> Drop this into `templates/client_agent/client_agent.py` in the **template repo**, replacing the previous version. The spawner will copy it into each client root.
> 
> Key changes:
> 
> - Adds **`PATTERN_RULES`** tuned to your flat structure  
> - Adds **`normalize_filename`**  
> - Adds **`organize`**: auto-move + auto-rename according to pattern rules  
> - Still has `validate`, `compact`, `report`, `build_index`  
> 
> ```python
> #!/usr/bin/env python3
> """
> QiAlly Client Agent (flat, portable)
> 
> Commands:
>   validate    : check structure, depth, large files
>   compact     : move large files to archive and leave pointers
>   report      : generate simple HTML health report
>   build_index : build lightweight JSON index for the portal RAG search
>   organize    : auto-rename & auto-move files based on pattern rules
> 
> Usage:
>   python client_agent.py validate
>   python client_agent.py compact
>   python client_agent.py report
>   python client_agent.py build_index
>   python client_agent.py organize          # live
>   python client_agent.py organize --dry    # dry run
> """
> 
> import sys
> import json
> import shutil
> import re
> from pathlib import Path
> from datetime import datetime
> 
> ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parent
> META_PATH = ROOT / "client.meta.json"
> 
> REQUIRED_TOP_LEVEL = [
>     "_system",
>     "10_profile",
>     "20_engagement",
>     "30_ops",
>     "40_finance",
>     "50_work",
>     "60_kb",
>     "70_archive",
>     "kb_site",
>     "portal",
> ]
> 
> LARGE_FILE_MB = 25
> MAX_DEPTH = 4
> 
> # ---------- PATTERN RULES (AUTO CLASSIFICATION) ----------
> 
> PATTERN_RULES = [
>     # Profile / IDs
>     {
>         "label": "Profile IDs",
>         "contains_any": ["passport", "license", "driver", "national-id", "id-card", "ssn", "social-security"],
>         "dest": "10_profile/ids",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Profile Personal",
>         "contains_any": ["resume", "cv", "profile", "bio"],
>         "dest": "10_profile/personal",
>     },
> 
>     # Engagement
>     {
>         "label": "Engagement Proposals",
>         "contains_any": ["proposal", "quote", "estimate", "offer"],
>         "dest": "20_engagement/proposals",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Engagement Contracts",
>         "contains_any": ["contract", "agreement", "msa", "sow", "work-order", "work order"],
>         "dest": "20_engagement/contracts",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Engagement Scope",
>         "contains_any": ["scope", "statement-of-work", "sow-scope"],
>         "dest": "20_engagement/scope",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Engagement Policies",
>         "contains_any": ["policy", "policies", "terms", "conditions", "privacy", "tos"],
>         "dest": "20_engagement/policies",
>     },
> 
>     # Ops
>     {
>         "label": "Ops Onboarding",
>         "contains_any": ["onboarding", "intake"],
>         "dest": "30_ops/onboarding",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Ops Access",
>         "contains_any": ["access", "credentials", "login", "password"],
>         "dest": "30_ops/access",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Ops Checklists",
>         "contains_any": ["checklist", "todo", "task-list"],
>         "dest": "30_ops/checklists",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Ops SOPs",
>         "contains_any": ["sop", "procedure", "playbook"],
>         "dest": "30_ops/sops",
>     },
> 
>     # Finance
>     {
>         "label": "Finance Invoices",
>         "contains_any": ["invoice", "inv_", "inv-"],
>         "dest": "40_finance/invoices",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Finance Expenses",
>         "contains_any": ["receipt", "receipts", "expense", "reimbursement"],
>         "dest": "40_finance/expenses",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Finance Bank",
>         "contains_any": ["bank", "statement", "deposit", "withdrawal", "payout"],
>         "dest": "40_finance/bank",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Finance Tax",
>         "contains_any": ["tax", "1040", "w2", "1099", "schedule-c", "schedule_c", "schc", "sch_c"],
>         "dest": "40_finance/tax",
>     },
> 
>     # Work - Immigration
>     {
>         "label": "Work Immigration",
>         "contains_any": ["i-589", "i589", "i-360", "i360", "i-130", "i130", "ds-260", "ds260", "uscis", "rfe"],
>         "dest": "50_work/immigration",
>     },
> 
>     # Work - Marketing
>     {
>         "label": "Work Marketing",
>         "contains_any": ["campaign", "adset", "creative", "landing", "funnel", "brief"],
>         "dest": "50_work/marketing",
>     },
> 
>     # Work - Generic Projects
>     {
>         "label": "Work Projects",
>         "contains_any": ["project", "deliverable", "timeline", "milestone", "plan", "strategy", "spec"],
>         "dest": "50_work/projects",
>     },
> 
>     # KB / References
>     {
>         "label": "KB Notes",
>         "contains_any": ["notes", "meeting", "minutes", "summary", "journal"],
>         "dest": "60_kb/kb_vault",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "KB Guides",
>         "contains_any": ["guide", "manual", "how-to", "howto", "faq"],
>         "dest": "60_kb/references",
>     },
> 
>     # Legal general
>     {
>         "label": "Legal Docs",
>         "contains_any": ["lawsuit", "complaint", "subpoena", "summons", "court", "case-no", "case_"],
>         "dest": "60_kb/legal",
>     },
> 
>     # Media (by extension)
>     {
>         "label": "Media Images/Videos",
>         "extensions": [".png", ".jpg", ".jpeg", ".gif", ".heic", ".mp4", ".mov", ".m4a", ".mp3", ".wav"],
>         "dest": "60_kb/media",
>     },
> ]
> 
> TOP_LEVELS = {p.split("/")[0] for p in REQUIRED_TOP_LEVEL}
> 
> 
> def load_meta() -> dict:
>     if META_PATH.exists():
>         try:
>             return json.loads(META_PATH.read_text(encoding="utf-8"))
>         except Exception:
>             pass
>     return {}
> 
> 
> def normalize_filename(filename: str) -> str:
>     p = Path(filename)
>     stem = p.stem.lower()
>     ext = p.suffix.lower()
> 
>     stem = re.sub(r"[ \t]+", "-", stem)
>     stem = re.sub(r"[\\/]+", "-", stem)
>     stem = re.sub(r"[^a-z0-9\-_]+", "-", stem)
>     stem = re.sub(r"-{2,}", "-", stem).strip("-")
> 
>     if not stem:
>         stem = "file"
>     return stem + ext
> 
> 
> def within_managed_area(path: Path) -> bool:
>     """Return True if already under one of our managed top-level folders."""
>     try:
>         rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>     except ValueError:
>         return False
>     if not rel.parts:
>         return False
>     return rel.parts[0] in TOP_LEVELS
> 
> 
> def classify_destination(path: Path) -> str | None:
>     """
>     Decide where a file should go based on PATTERN_RULES.
> 
>     Returns dest relative path (folder) or None if no rule applied.
>     """
>     name = path.name.lower()
>     ext = path.suffix.lower()
>     full = str(path.name).lower()
> 
>     for rule in PATTERN_RULES:
>         # Extension-based rule
>         exts = rule.get("extensions")
>         if exts and ext in exts:
>             return rule["dest"]
> 
>         terms = rule.get("contains_any", [])
>         if terms:
>             if any(t in full for t in terms):
>                 return rule["dest"]
> 
>     # Default fallback: references
>     return "60_kb/references"
> 
> 
> # --------- existing commands: validate / compact / report / build_index ---------
> # (same as earlier, but using new constants; I’ll keep them as-is for brevity)
> 
> def validate() -> int:
>     print("=== VALIDATE ===")
>     meta = load_meta()
>     if meta:
>         print(f"Client: {meta.get('client_name', 'Unknown')} ({meta.get('client_code', 'c.unknown')})")
>         print(f"QID   : {meta.get('qid', 'N/A')}")
>     else:
>         print("WARN: client.meta.json missing or unreadable.")
> 
>     print("\n[1] Top-level folders")
>     for name in REQUIRED_TOP_LEVEL:
>         p = ROOT / name
>         if not p.exists():
>             print(f"  - MISSING : {name}")
>         else:
>             print(f"  - OK      : {name}")
> 
>     print("\n[2] Orphan files at root")
>     ignored = {"client.meta.json", "README.md", "client_agent.py"}
>     for item in ROOT.iterdir():
>         if item.is_file() and item.name not in ignored:
>             print(f"  - ORPHAN FILE: {item.name}")
> 
>     print(f"\n[3] Depth check (>{MAX_DEPTH} levels)")
>     too_deep = []
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if path.is_dir():
>             continue
>         rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>         depth = len(rel.parts)
>         if depth > MAX_DEPTH:
>             too_deep.append(str(rel))
> 
>     if too_deep:
>         print(f"Found {len(too_deep)} items deeper than {MAX_DEPTH} levels:")
>         for rel in too_deep[:20]:
>             print(f"  - {rel}")
>         if len(too_deep) > 20:
>             print(f"  ... +{len(too_deep) - 20} more")
>     else:
>         print("No paths beyond depth limit.")
> 
>     print(f"\n[4] Large files (>{LARGE_FILE_MB} MB)")
>     large = []
>     threshold = LARGE_FILE_MB * 1024 * 1024
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if path.is_file():
>             try:
>                 size = path.stat().st_size
>             except OSError:
>                 continue
>             if size >= threshold:
>                 large.append((path, size))
> 
>     if large:
>         for path, size in sorted(large, key=lambda x: x[1], reverse=True):
>             rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>             mb = size / (1024 * 1024)
>             print(f"  - {rel} ({mb:.1f} MB)")
>     else:
>         print("No large files found.")
> 
>     print("\n[✓] Validation complete.\n")
>     return 0
> 
> 
> def compact() -> int:
>     print("=== COMPACT ===")
>     archive_root = ROOT / "70_archive"
>     archive_root.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
> 
>     large_assets_dir = archive_root / "large_assets"
>     large_assets_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
> 
>     threshold = LARGE_FILE_MB * 1024 * 1024
>     moved = 0
> 
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if not path.is_file():
>             continue
>         if path.is_relative_to(archive_root):
>             continue
>         if path.name in {"client.meta.json", "client_agent.py"}:
>             continue
> 
>         try:
>             size = path.stat().st_size
>         except OSError:
>             continue
> 
>         if size >= threshold:
>             rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>             target = large_assets_dir / rel
>             target.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>             print(f"  - Moving large file to archive: {rel}")
>             shutil.move(str(path), str(target))
>             moved += 1
> 
>             pointer_path = ROOT / rel
>             pointer_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>             pointer_path.write_text(
>                 f"This file was moved to archive:\n"
>                 f"  70_archive/large_assets/{rel}\n"
>                 f"Size: {size / (1024*1024):.1f} MB\n",
>                 encoding="utf-8",
>             )
> 
>     print(f"\n[✓] Compact complete. Large files moved: {moved}\n")
>     return 0
> 
> 
> def report() -> int:
>     print("=== REPORT ===")
>     meta = load_meta()
>     now = datetime.utcnow().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S UTC")
>     summary = {
>         "generated_at": now,
>         "client": {
>             "name": meta.get("client_name", "Unknown"),
>             "code": meta.get("client_code", "c.unknown"),
>             "qid": meta.get("qid", "N/A"),
>         },
>         "folders": {},
>         "largest_files": [],
>     }
> 
>     for top in ROOT.iterdir():
>         if not top.is_dir():
>             continue
>         size = 0
>         count = 0
>         for path in top.rglob("*"):
>             if path.is_file():
>                 try:
>                     size += path.stat().st_size
>                     count += 1
>                 except OSError:
>                     continue
>         summary["folders"][top.name] = {
>             "files": count,
>             "size_bytes": size,
>         }
> 
>     all_files = []
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if path.is_file():
>             try:
>                 size = path.stat().st_size
>             except OSError:
>                 continue
>             all_files.append((path, size))
> 
>     top_n = sorted(all_files, key=lambda x: x[1], reverse=True)[:20]
>     for path, size in top_n:
>         rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>         summary["largest_files"].append(
>             {"path": str(rel), "size_bytes": size}
>         )
> 
>     reports_dir = ROOT / "70_archive" / "reports"
>     reports_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>     ts = datetime.utcnow().strftime("%Y%m%d_%H%M%S")
>     html_path = reports_dir / f"health_{ts}.html"
> 
>     def fmt_size(b: int) -> str:
>         mb = b / (1024 * 1024)
>         return f"{mb:.1f} MB"
> 
>     lines = []
>     lines.append("<!DOCTYPE html>")
>     lines.append("<html><head><meta charset='utf-8'><title>Client Health Report</title>")
>     lines.append("<style>body{font-family:sans-serif;max-width:900px;margin:2rem auto;} table{border-collapse:collapse;width:100%;} th,td{border:1px solid #ccc;padding:4px 8px;text-align:left;} h1,h2{margin-top:1.5rem;}</style>")
>     lines.append("</head><body>")
>     lines.append("<h1>Client Health Report</h1>")
>     lines.append(f"<p>Generated: {now}</p>")
>     lines.append(f"<p>Client: {summary['client']['name']} ({summary['client']['code']}) – QID: {summary['client']['qid']}</p>")
> 
>     lines.append("<h2>Folder Summary</h2>")
>     lines.append("<table><tr><th>Folder</th><th>Files</th><th>Size</th></tr>")
>     for name, info in sorted(summary["folders"].items()):
>         lines.append(f"<tr><td>{name}</td><td>{info['files']}</td><td>{fmt_size(info['size_bytes'])}</td></tr>")
>     lines.append("</table>")
> 
>     lines.append("<h2>Largest Files</h2>")
>     if summary["largest_files"]:
>         lines.append("<table><tr><th>Path</th><th>Size</th></tr>")
>         for item in summary["largest_files"]:
>             lines.append(f"<tr><td>{item['path']}</td><td>{fmt_size(item['size_bytes'])}</td></tr>")
>         lines.append("</table>")
>     else:
>         lines.append("<p>No files found.</p>")
> 
>     lines.append("</body></html>")
>     html_path.write_text("\n".join(lines), encoding="utf-8")
> 
>     print(f"[✓] Report written to: {html_path}")
>     return 0
> 
> 
> # --------- RAG index builder (for portal) ---------
> 
> def extract_text(path: Path) -> str:
>     try:
>         text = path.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")
>     except Exception:
>         return ""
> 
>     if path.suffix.lower() in {".md", ".txt"}:
>         return text
> 
>     if path.suffix.lower() in {".html", ".htm"}:
>         import re as _re
>         return _re.sub(r"<[^>]+>", " ", text)
> 
>     return ""
> 
> 
> def build_index() -> int:
>     print("=== BUILD INDEX ===")
>     kb_root = ROOT / "60_kb" / "kb_vault"
>     work_root = ROOT / "50_work"
>     docs = []
> 
>     for base in [kb_root, work_root]:
>         if not base.exists():
>             continue
>         for path in base.rglob("*"):
>             if not path.is_file():
>                 continue
>             if path.suffix.lower() not in {".md", ".txt", ".html", ".htm"}:
>                 continue
> 
>             rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>             text = extract_text(path)
>             if not text.strip():
>                 continue
> 
>             snippet = " ".join(text.split()[:80])
> 
>             docs.append({
>                 "id": str(rel),
>                 "title": path.stem,
>                 "path": str(rel),
>                 "snippet": snippet,
>                 "content": text,
>             })
> 
>     portal_data = ROOT / "portal" / "data"
>     portal_data.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>     index_path = portal_data / "docs_index.json"
>     index_path.write_text(json.dumps(docs, indent=2), encoding="utf-8")
> 
>     print(f"[✓] Indexed {len(docs)} docs into {index_path}")
>     return 0
> 
> 
> # --------- ORGANIZE (auto move + rename) ---------
> 
> def organize(dry: bool = False) -> int:
>     """
>     Auto-rename & auto-move files based on PATTERN_RULES.
> 
>     - Skips:
>         * _system, kb_site, portal, 70_archive
>         * files already under known top-levels in correct place
>         * client.meta.json, client_agent.py
>     - Normalizes filenames.
>     """
>     print("=== ORGANIZE ===")
>     print(f"Dry run: {dry}")
>     moved = 0
> 
>     skip_roots = {"_system", "kb_site", "portal", "70_archive"}
> 
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if not path.is_file():
>             continue
> 
>         if path.name in {"client.meta.json", "client_agent.py"}:
>             continue
> 
>         rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>         parts = rel.parts
>         if not parts:
>             continue
> 
>         top = parts[0]
> 
>         # Don't reorganize system/portal/archive
>         if top in skip_roots:
>             continue
> 
>         # If already under one of our top-levels, we still may move deeper
>         # but we won't move if it *already* seems correctly classified.
>         if top in TOP_LEVELS and len(parts) > 1:
>             # Leave things under top-level that are already structured
>             # (we assume "good enough" to avoid thrashing)
>             continue
> 
>         dest_folder = classify_destination(path)
>         new_name = normalize_filename(path.name)
>         dest_rel = Path(dest_folder) / new_name
>         dest_abs = ROOT / dest_rel
>         dest_abs.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
> 
>         if dry:
>             print(f"[DRY] {rel}  ->  {dest_rel}")
>             continue
> 
>         # Avoid overwrite: if exists, append __DUPn
>         candidate = dest_abs
>         if candidate.exists():
>             stem = candidate.stem
>             ext = candidate.suffix
>             n = 1
>             while True:
>                 dup_name = f"{stem}__DUP{n}{ext}"
>                 candidate = dest_abs.with_name(dup_name)
>                 if not candidate.exists():
>                     break
>                 n += 1
>         print(f"  MOVE {rel}  ->  {candidate.relative_to(ROOT)}")
>         shutil.move(str(path), str(candidate))
>         moved += 1
> 
>     print(f"\n[✓] Organize complete. Files moved: {moved} (dry={dry})\n")
>     return 0
> 
> 
> def main(argv: list[str]) -> int:
>     if len(argv) < 2:
>         print("Usage: python client_agent.py [validate|compact|report|build_index|organize]")
>         return 1
> 
>     cmd = argv[1].lower()
>     if cmd == "validate":
>         return validate()
>     if cmd == "compact":
>         return compact()
>     if cmd == "report":
>         return report()
>     if cmd == "build_index":
>         return build_index()
>     if cmd == "organize":
>         dry = len(argv) > 2 and argv[2] in {"--dry", "--dry-run"}
>         return organize(dry=dry)
> 
>     print(f"Unknown command: {cmd}")
>     return 1
> 
> 
> if __name__ == "__main__":
>     raise SystemExit(main(sys.argv))
> ```
> 
> Usage in a client repo:
> 
> ```bash
> python client_agent.py organize --dry   # see what it *would* do
> python client_agent.py organize         # actually move + rename
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. “Mini Gina” – portal chat with optional nano-LLM
> 
> You asked for a tiny Gina living in the client repo. With your constraints (HTML5, offline, light), here’s the honest reality:
> 
> - A **real** LLM in-browser (WebLLM, transformers.js) is heavy as hell.  
> - What we *can* do cleanly:
>   - Use the **docs index** (`docs_index.json`) as our RAG pool.
>   - Implement a **chat UI** that:
>     - Pulls relevant docs.
>     - Shows stitched context + answers with a rule-based template.
>   - Add an **optional hook** to a local LLM endpoint (e.g. Ollama at `http://localhost:11434`) if you want actual generation.
> 
> So Mini Gina has two modes:
> 
> 1. **Pure offline / no LLM** → RAG + template answers (still useful).
> 2. **Local LLM mode** → same RAG, but it POSTs to `LLM_ENDPOINT` running on your machine.
> 
> ### Portal chat wiring
> 
> Inside `portal/index.html`, add a chat section and include `js/chat.js`:
> 
> ```html
> <section>
>   <h2>Chat with Mini Gina</h2>
>   <div id="chat">
>     <div id="chat-log" style="border:1px solid #ccc; padding:0.5rem; height:250px; overflow-y:auto; font-size:0.9rem;"></div>
>     <div style="margin-top:0.5rem;">
>       <input id="chat-input" type="text" placeholder="Ask a question..." style="width:80%;" />
>       <button id="chat-send">Send</button>
>     </div>
>     <small style="color:#666;">
>       Mini Gina uses your client docs index. For true AI responses, configure a local LLM endpoint in chat.js.
>     </small>
>   </div>
> </section>
> 
> <script src="js/search.js"></script>
> <script src="js/chat.js"></script>
> ```
> 
> Then create `portal/js/chat.js`:
> 
> ```javascript
> (function () {
>   const logEl = document.getElementById("chat-log");
>   const inputEl = document.getElementById("chat-input");
>   const sendBtn = document.getElementById("chat-send");
> 
>   // Optional local LLM endpoint. Leave null for "template-only" mode.
>   // Example for Ollama: "http://localhost:11434/api/generate"
>   const LLM_ENDPOINT = null;
> 
>   let docs = [];
> 
>   async function loadIndex() {
>     try {
>       const res = await fetch("data/docs_index.json", { cache: "no-store" });
>       if (!res.ok) throw new Error("Failed to load docs index");
>       docs = await res.json();
>       console.log("[Mini Gina] Loaded docs index:", docs.length, "docs");
>     } catch (err) {
>       console.error(err);
>       appendSystem("Could not load docs index. Run: client_agent.py build_index");
>     }
>   }
> 
>   function appendMessage(who, text) {
>     const div = document.createElement("div");
>     div.style.marginBottom = "0.5rem";
>     const label = who === "user" ? "You" : "Mini Gina";
>     div.innerHTML = `<strong>${label}:</strong> ${text}`;
>     logEl.appendChild(div);
>     logEl.scrollTop = logEl.scrollHeight;
>   }
> 
>   function appendSystem(text) {
>     const div = document.createElement("div");
>     div.style.marginBottom = "0.5rem";
>     div.style.color = "#666";
>     div.innerHTML = `<em>${text}</em>`;
>     logEl.appendChild(div);
>     logEl.scrollTop = logEl.scrollHeight;
>   }
> 
>   function scoreDoc(doc, terms) {
>     const text = (doc.content || "").toLowerCase();
>     let score = 0;
>     for (const t of terms) {
>       if (!t) continue;
>       const occurrences = text.split(t).length - 1;
>       score += occurrences;
>     }
>     return score;
>   }
> 
>   function findRelevantDocs(question) {
>     const q = question.toLowerCase();
>     const terms = q.split(/\s+/).filter(Boolean);
>     const scored = docs
>       .map((d) => ({ doc: d, score: scoreDoc(d, terms) }))
>       .filter((x) => x.score > 0)
>       .sort((a, b) => b.score - a.score);
>     return scored.slice(0, 5).map((x) => x.doc);
>   }
> 
>   function buildContext(question, relevant) {
>     let ctx = `Question: ${question}\n\nRelevant documents:\n`;
>     relevant.forEach((d, i) => {
>       ctx += `\n[${i + 1}] ${d.title} (${d.path})\n${d.snippet}\n`;
>     });
>     return ctx;
>   }
> 
>   function templateAnswer(question, relevant) {
>     if (!relevant.length) {
>       return "I didn’t find anything in this client’s docs that clearly matches that. Try rephrasing or be more specific.";
>     }
>     let answer = "Here’s what I’m seeing in this client’s docs that seems related:\n\n";
>     relevant.forEach((d, i) => {
>       answer += `${i + 1}. ${d.title} (${d.path})\n   ${d.snippet}\n\n`;
>     });
>     answer += "Open the linked docs above directly for full details.";
>     return answer;
>   }
> 
>   async function askLocalLLM(context, question) {
>     if (!LLM_ENDPOINT) {
>       return null;
>     }
>     try {
>       const payload = {
>         prompt: `You are Mini Gina, a concise assistant answering questions about a specific client using the provided context.\n\nContext:\n${context}\n\nQuestion: ${question}\n\nAnswer briefly, in plain language:`,
>         // This payload shape will vary by LLM server; adjust as needed.
>       };
>       const res = await fetch(LLM_ENDPOINT, {
>         method: "POST",
>         headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },
>         body: JSON.stringify(payload),
>       });
>       if (!res.ok) throw new Error("LLM request failed");
>       const data = await res.json();
>       // You will need to adapt this to your chosen LLM API's response shape.
>       return data.response || data.choices?.[0]?.text || null;
>     } catch (err) {
>       console.error(err);
>       return null;
>     }
>   }
> 
>   async function handleSend() {
>     const q = (inputEl.value || "").trim();
>     if (!q) return;
>     inputEl.value = "";
>     appendMessage("user", q);
> 
>     if (!docs.length) {
>       appendSystem("Index not loaded. Run: client_agent.py build_index");
>       return;
>     }
> 
>     const relevant = findRelevantDocs(q);
>     const context = buildContext(q, relevant);
> 
>     // Try local LLM if configured
>     let answer = null;
>     if (LLM_ENDPOINT) {
>       appendSystem("Thinking via local LLM...");
>       answer = await askLocalLLM(context, q);
>     }
> 
>     if (!answer) {
>       // Fallback: rule-based RAG answer
>       answer = templateAnswer(q, relevant);
>     }
> 
>     appendMessage("gina", answer);
>   }
> 
>   sendBtn.addEventListener("click", handleSend);
>   inputEl.addEventListener("keydown", (e) => {
>     if (e.key === "Enter") handleSend();
>   });
> 
>   loadIndex();
> })();
> ```
> 
> So:
> 
> - With **no LLM configured**, Mini Gina = smart “search + summarize” over your client docs.  
> - If you point `LLM_ENDPOINT` at some local nano-LLM you’re running (Ollama, llamafile, whatever), she becomes a real chat agent while still staying **local + portal-based**.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## How this all fits together
> 
> Template repo (`qi-client-template`) has:
> 
> - `client_spawner.py` + `start.sh`
> - `templates/`:
>   - `kb_site/` (HTML5 shell)
>   - `portal_shell/` (`index.html`, `js/search.js`, `js/chat.js`, `data/`)
>   - `client_agent/client_agent.py`
>   - `kb_vault_seed/`, `system_templates/`, etc.
> 
> Spawner:
> 
> - Copies these into the new client repo.  
> - Writes `client.meta.json`.  
> - Adds them to `qi_client_registry.json` in the template repo.
> 
> Client agent:
> 
> - `python client_agent.py validate`
> - `python client_agent.py organize --dry`
> - `python client_agent.py organize`
> - `python client_agent.py compact`
> - `python client_agent.py build_index`
> - `python client_agent.py report`
> 
> Portal:
> 
> - Open `portal/index.html` →  
>   - Search + RAG list, plus  
>   - Mini Gina chat over those same docs.
> 
> If you want next, we can tighten the **pattern rules for specific clients** (like a “legal-heavy” profile vs a “marketing-only” profile) and make the agent choose a rule-set based on a flag in `client.meta.json` (e.g. `"profile": "immigration"` vs `"profile": "construction"`).

### User
> yes lets do that and also we need to make sure the spawner or agent is checking for git repo for the client or creating one automatcially if none is there then optionally pushing once the spawn or audit is done, and of course the deployment of the kb site and marketing site with the clients info and color schema and logo, so it will need to look for a clogo or create a logo, we can use maybe a light api and static prompt to have the log made and retrieve it or am i doing to much now.

### Assistant
> Yeah, you’re doing a lot 😏 — but it’s still manageable if we **layer it** instead of shoving everything into one ball of chaos.
> 
> Let’s treat it as three tiers:
> 
> 1. **Core** – spawn structure, agent, RAG index (already done).  
> 2. **Smart** – profile-specific pattern rules + git repo handling.  
> 3. **Bougie** – branding (colors + logo) + deployment scripts + optional logo API.
> 
> I’ll give you **concrete code** you can drop in, without bloating the whole thing.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1. Profile-based pattern rules (immigration vs construction vs generic)
> 
> We’ll make the agent choose pattern rules based on `client.meta.json`:
> 
> ```json
> {
>   "client_name": "Built By Rays Construction",
>   "client_code": "c.bbr",
>   "qid": "QCL-20251206-ABCD",
>   "profile_type": "construction",   // <--- key field
>   "brand": {
>     "primary": "#004b8d",
>     "secondary": "#f4a300",
>     "accent": "#222222",
>     "logo_path": "60_kb/media/logo.png",
>     "source": "provided"            // or "generated"
>   }
> }
> ```
> 
> ### In `client_agent.py`: rule sets per profile
> 
> Replace the previous single `PATTERN_RULES` with this:
> 
> ```python
> # ---------- PATTERN RULE SETS (BY PROFILE TYPE) ----------
> 
> GENERIC_RULES = [
>     # (your existing generic rules, slightly trimmed)
>     {
>         "label": "Profile IDs",
>         "contains_any": ["passport", "license", "driver", "national-id", "id-card", "ssn", "social-security"],
>         "dest": "10_profile/ids",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Profile Personal",
>         "contains_any": ["resume", "cv", "profile", "bio"],
>         "dest": "10_profile/personal",
>     },
>     # ... Engagement, Ops, Finance, KB, Legal, Media, etc (what we already wrote) ...
> ]
> 
> IMMIGRATION_EXTRA_RULES = [
>     {
>         "label": "Immigration Core Forms",
>         "contains_any": ["i-589", "i589", "i-360", "i360", "i-130", "i130", "ds-260", "ds260", "uscis", "rfe"],
>         "dest": "50_work/immigration",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Country Evidence",
>         "contains_any": ["country-conditions", "unhcr", "state-dept", "human-rights", "hrw", "amnesty"],
>         "dest": "50_work/immigration",
>     },
> ]
> 
> CONSTRUCTION_EXTRA_RULES = [
>     {
>         "label": "Construction Estimates/Proposals",
>         "contains_any": ["estimate", "proposal", "bid", "quote", "scope-of-work", "sow"],
>         "dest": "50_work/projects",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Construction Photos",
>         "contains_any": ["roof", "siding", "gutter", "before", "after", "jobsite"],
>         "dest": "50_work/projects",
>     },
>     {
>         "label": "Construction Invoices",
>         "contains_any": ["invoice", "statement", "draw", "progress-invoice"],
>         "dest": "40_finance/invoices",
>     },
> ]
> 
> PROFILE_RULE_SETS = {
>     "generic": GENERIC_RULES,
>     "immigration": GENERIC_RULES + IMMIGRATION_EXTRA_RULES,
>     "construction": GENERIC_RULES + CONSTRUCTION_EXTRA_RULES,
> }
> ```
> 
> Then add a helper:
> 
> ```python
> def get_profile_type(meta: dict) -> str:
>     t = (meta.get("profile_type") or "generic").lower()
>     if t not in PROFILE_RULE_SETS:
>         return "generic"
>     return t
> 
> 
> def get_pattern_rules(meta: dict) -> list[dict]:
>     t = get_profile_type(meta)
>     return PROFILE_RULE_SETS[t]
> ```
> 
> Update `classify_destination` to use `meta`:
> 
> ```python
> def classify_destination(path: Path, meta: dict) -> str:
>     """
>     Decide where a file should go based on PROFILE_RULE_SETS.
>     Returns dest folder (str).
>     """
>     rules = get_pattern_rules(meta)
>     name = path.name.lower()
>     ext = path.suffix.lower()
>     full = name
> 
>     for rule in rules:
>         exts = rule.get("extensions")
>         if exts and ext in exts:
>             return rule["dest"]
> 
>         terms = rule.get("contains_any", [])
>         if terms and any(t in full for t in terms):
>             return rule["dest"]
> 
>     return "60_kb/references"
> ```
> 
> And in `organize`:
> 
> ```python
> def organize(dry: bool = False) -> int:
>     print("=== ORGANIZE ===")
>     meta = load_meta()
>     profile_type = get_profile_type(meta)
>     print(f"Profile type: {profile_type}")
>     print(f"Dry run: {dry}")
> 
>     moved = 0
>     skip_roots = {"_system", "kb_site", "portal", "70_archive"}
> 
>     for path in ROOT.rglob("*"):
>         if not path.is_file():
>             continue
>         if path.name in {"client.meta.json", "client_agent.py"}:
>             continue
> 
>         rel = path.relative_to(ROOT)
>         parts = rel.parts
>         if not parts:
>             continue
> 
>         top = parts[0]
>         if top in skip_roots:
>             continue
>         if top in TOP_LEVELS and len(parts) > 1:
>             # already in a subfolder; don't thrash
>             continue
> 
>         dest_folder = classify_destination(path, meta)
>         new_name = normalize_filename(path.name)
>         dest_rel = Path(dest_folder) / new_name
>         dest_abs = ROOT / dest_rel
>         dest_abs.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
> 
>         if dry:
>             print(f"[DRY] {rel}  ->  {dest_rel}")
>             continue
> 
>         candidate = dest_abs
>         if candidate.exists():
>             stem = candidate.stem
>             ext = candidate.suffix
>             n = 1
>             while True:
>                 dup_name = f"{stem}__DUP{n}{ext}"
>                 candidate = dest_abs.with_name(dup_name)
>                 if not candidate.exists():
>                     break
>                 n += 1
> 
>         print(f"  MOVE {rel}  ->  {candidate.relative_to(ROOT)}")
>         shutil.move(str(path), str(candidate))
>         moved += 1
> 
>     print(f"\n[✓] Organize complete. Files moved: {moved} (dry={dry})\n")
>     return 0
> ```
> 
> Now the **same agent** behaves differently per client just by `profile_type`.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. Git repo handling (init + optional push)
> 
> This belongs in **`client_spawner.py`** (template repo).
> 
> Add:
> 
> ```python
> import subprocess
> 
> def is_git_repo(path: Path) -> bool:
>     return (path / ".git").exists()
> 
> 
> def run_cmd(cmd: list[str], cwd: Path) -> bool:
>     try:
>         subprocess.run(cmd, cwd=str(cwd), check=True)
>         return True
>     except Exception as e:
>         print(f"  [git] command failed: {' '.join(cmd)} -> {e}")
>         return False
> 
> 
> def ensure_git_repo(client_root: Path) -> None:
>     print("\n--- Git Setup ---")
>     if is_git_repo(client_root):
>         print("Git repo already exists here; skipping git init.")
>         return
> 
>     ans = input("Initialize a new git repo for this client? [y/N]: ").strip().lower()
>     if ans != "y":
>         print("Skipping git init.")
>         return
> 
>     if not run_cmd(["git", "init"], client_root):
>         return
>     if not run_cmd(["git", "add", "."], client_root):
>         return
>     if not run_cmd(["git", "commit", "-m", "Initial QiAlly client scaffold"], client_root):
>         return
> 
>     print("Git repo initialized and initial commit created.")
> 
>     ans = input("Configure remote & push now? [y/N]: ").strip().lower()
>     if ans != "y":
>         print("Skipping remote/push config.")
>         return
> 
>     remote_url = input("Remote URL (e.g. git@github.com:qiallyme/c.bbr.git): ").strip()
>     if not remote_url:
>         print("No remote URL provided; skipping.")
>         return
> 
>     if not run_cmd(["git", "remote", "add", "origin", remote_url], client_root):
>         return
> 
>     default_branch = input("Default branch name [main]: ").strip() or "main"
>     run_cmd(["git", "branch", "-M", default_branch], client_root)
>     run_cmd(["git", "push", "-u", "origin", default_branch], client_root)
>     print("Remote configured & initial push attempted.")
> ```
> 
> Then, after you finish scaffolding a new client in the spawner:
> 
> ```python
> # pseudo inside "new client" path
> client_root = Path(target_path).resolve()
> # ... create folders, copy templates, write client.meta.json, etc ...
> ensure_git_repo(client_root)
> ```
> 
> This gives you:
> 
> - Auto-create git repo if none.
> - Optional remote + push.  
> - Still light and explicit—no magic.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Branding, color scheme, logo detection/generation
> 
> You’re not crazy; you’re just stacking concerns. We’ll keep this *optional* and mostly **config + templates**.
> 
> ### 3.1. Branding schema in `client.meta.json`
> 
> On spawn, ask:
> 
> - “Do you have branding colors already? [y/N]”
> - “Do you have a logo file for this client? [path or leave blank]”
> 
> And then write to meta:
> 
> ```python
> DEFAULT_BRAND_PALETTES = [
>     {"primary": "#004b8d", "secondary": "#f4a300", "accent": "#222222"},
>     {"primary": "#1b4965", "secondary": "#ffd166", "accent": "#202020"},
>     {"primary": "#0b7285", "secondary": "#ff922b", "accent": "#343a40"},
> ]
> 
> def pick_default_palette() -> dict:
>     # simple deterministic pick could be based on hash of client_code
>     import hashlib
>     idx = 0
>     try:
>         h = hashlib.sha1()
>         h.update(client_code.encode("utf-8"))
>         idx = int(h.hexdigest(), 16) % len(DEFAULT_BRAND_PALETTES)
>     except Exception:
>         pass
>     return DEFAULT_BRAND_PALETTES[idx].copy()
> ```
> 
> Then in spawner’s new-client flow:
> 
> ```python
> brand = {}
> 
> use_custom = input("Use custom brand colors? [y/N]: ").strip().lower() == "y"
> if use_custom:
>     p = input("Primary color (hex, e.g. #004b8d) [#004b8d]: ").strip() or "#004b8d"
>     s = input("Secondary color (hex) [#f4a300]: ").strip() or "#f4a300"
>     a = input("Accent color (hex) [#222222]: ").strip() or "#222222"
>     brand = {"primary": p, "secondary": s, "accent": a}
> else:
>     brand = pick_default_palette()
> 
> logo_path = input("Path to client logo file (optional): ").strip()
> if logo_path:
>     # copy it into 60_kb/media/logo.ext
>     logo_src = Path(logo_path).expanduser().resolve()
>     logo_dest_dir = client_root / "60_kb" / "media"
>     logo_dest_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>     logo_dest = logo_dest_dir / f"logo{logo_src.suffix.lower()}"
>     shutil.copy2(logo_src, logo_dest)
>     logo_path_rel = str(logo_dest.relative_to(client_root))
> else:
>     logo_path_rel = ""
> 
> meta = {
>     "client_name": client_name,
>     "client_code": client_code,
>     "qid": qid,
>     "profile_type": profile_type,
>     "brand": {
>         "primary": brand["primary"],
>         "secondary": brand["secondary"],
>         "accent": brand["accent"],
>         "logo_path": logo_path_rel,
>         "source": "provided" if logo_path_rel else "default",
>     },
>     # ... other fields ...
> }
> (client_root / "client.meta.json").write_text(json.dumps(meta, indent=2), encoding="utf-8")
> ```
> 
> ### 3.2. Apply brand to KB + portal CSS
> 
> In your template repo, keep CSS with **tokens**:
> 
> `templates/kb_site/css/style.css.tpl`:
> 
> ```css
> :root {
>   --primary: {{PRIMARY}};
>   --secondary: {{SECONDARY}};
>   --accent: {{ACCENT}};
> }
> body {
>   font-family: system-ui, -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, sans-serif;
>   color: #111;
>   background: #f8f9fa;
> }
> a { color: var(--primary); }
> ```
> 
> `templates/portal_shell/css/style.css.tpl` similarly.
> 
> Spawner writes the real CSS:
> 
> ```python
> def apply_brand_to_css(client_root: Path, meta: dict) -> None:
>     brand = meta.get("brand") or {}
>     primary = brand.get("primary", "#004b8d")
>     secondary = brand.get("secondary", "#f4a300")
>     accent = brand.get("accent", "#222222")
> 
>     replacements = {
>         "{{PRIMARY}}": primary,
>         "{{SECONDARY}}": secondary,
>         "{{ACCENT}}": accent,
>     }
> 
>     def render_tpl(tpl_path: Path, out_path: Path):
>         text = tpl_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
>         for k, v in replacements.items():
>             text = text.replace(k, v)
>         out_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>         out_path.write_text(text, encoding="utf-8")
> 
>     tpl_kb = TEMPLATE_ROOT / "kb_site" / "css" / "style.css.tpl"
>     tpl_portal = TEMPLATE_ROOT / "portal_shell" / "css" / "style.css.tpl"
>     if tpl_kb.exists():
>         render_tpl(tpl_kb, client_root / "kb_site" / "css" / "style.css")
>     if tpl_portal.exists():
>         render_tpl(tpl_portal, client_root / "portal" / "css" / "style.css")
> ```
> 
> Call `apply_brand_to_css(client_root, meta)` after meta is written and templates copied.
> 
> ### 3.3. Logo generation (optional, API-based)
> 
> This is where you *might* be doing too much, but we can stub it cleanly.
> 
> Idea:
> 
> - Environment variable: `QI_LOGO_API_URL` (your own tiny logo service, or some wrapper you build later).
> - If no logo provided and `QI_LOGO_API_URL` is set, spawner tries to generate.
> 
> In spawner:
> 
> ```python
> import os
> import requests  # you can make this optional if you want
> 
> def maybe_generate_logo(client_name: str, client_root: Path, brand: dict) -> str:
>     """
>     Try to generate a logo via external API.
>     Returns relative path to logo if created, else "".
>     """
>     api_url = os.environ.get("QI_LOGO_API_URL")
>     if not api_url:
>         print("No QI_LOGO_API_URL set; skipping logo generation.")
>         return ""
> 
>     payload = {
>         "client_name": client_name,
>         "primary_color": brand.get("primary"),
>         "secondary_color": brand.get("secondary"),
>         "accent_color": brand.get("accent"),
>         "style": "minimal, flat, circular mark, web-safe, no text outside symbol",
>     }
> 
>     try:
>         print("Requesting logo from logo API...")
>         res = requests.post(api_url, json=payload, timeout=30)
>         res.raise_for_status()
>         data = res.json()
>         # assume it returns a base64 PNG or a direct URL; you’ll define this.
>         if "logo_png_base64" in data:
>             import base64
>             raw = base64.b64decode(data["logo_png_base64"])
>             logo_dir = client_root / "60_kb" / "media"
>             logo_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>             logo_path = logo_dir / "logo.png"
>             logo_path.write_bytes(raw)
>             print(f"Logo generated at {logo_path}")
>             return str(logo_path.relative_to(client_root))
>         elif "logo_url" in data:
>             # if remote, you can download it here
>             logo_dir = client_root / "60_kb" / "media"
>             logo_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
>             logo_path = logo_dir / "logo.png"
>             r2 = requests.get(data["logo_url"], timeout=30)
>             r2.raise_for_status()
>             logo_path.write_bytes(r2.content)
>             print(f"Logo downloaded to {logo_path}")
>             return str(logo_path.relative_to(client_root))
>     except Exception as e:
>         print(f"Logo generation failed: {e}")
> 
>     return ""
> ```
> 
> Plug it into the branding flow:
> 
> - If user doesn’t provide logo path:
>   - Try `maybe_generate_logo`.
>   - If that fails, leave `logo_path` empty.
> 
> That keeps it **optional** and safely stubbed.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4. Deployment scripts (light, no magic)
> 
> Instead of trying to hit Cloudflare APIs directly from Python right now, just **prepare scripts** per client.
> 
> In spawner:
> 
> ```python
> def write_deploy_scripts(client_root: Path, meta: dict) -> None:
>     scripts_dir = client_root / "_system" / "scripts"
>     scripts_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
> 
>     kb_script = scripts_dir / "deploy_kb.sh"
>     portal_script = scripts_dir / "deploy_portal.sh"
> 
>     kb_script.write_text(
>         "#!/usr/bin/env bash\n"
>         "set -e\n"
>         'echo \"Deploying KB site...\"\n'
>         "cd \"$(dirname \"$0\")/../../kb_site\"\n"
>         "# TODO: adjust to your hosting. Example for Cloudflare Pages:\n"
>         "# npm install\n"
>         "# npm run build\n"
>         "# npx wrangler pages deploy dist --project-name=<PROJECT_NAME>\n",
>         encoding="utf-8",
>     )
>     portal_script.write_text(
>         "#!/usr/bin/env bash\n"
>         "set -e\n"
>         'echo \"Deploying Portal site...\"\n'
>         "cd \"$(dirname \"$0\")/../../portal\"\n"
>         "# TODO: adjust to your hosting.\n"
>         "# npm install (if needed)\n"
>         "# npx wrangler pages deploy . --project-name=<PORTAL_PROJECT>\n",
>         encoding="utf-8",
>     )
> 
>     kb_script.chmod(0o755)
>     portal_script.chmod(0o755)
>     print(f"Deploy scripts created in {scripts_dir}")
> ```
> 
> Call `write_deploy_scripts(client_root, meta)` as part of the new-client workflow.
> 
> You can wire these later into your CF setup. For now, it’s just consistent, per-client scripts sitting under `_system/scripts`.
>

> ## TL;DR What you actually need to do
> 
> 1. **Update template repo:**
>    - `client_agent.py` → add **profile-aware PATTERN_RULE_SETS** + `organize` uses meta.
>    - `client_spawner.py` → add:
>      - `ensure_git_repo`
>      - branding intake + meta writing
>      - `apply_brand_to_css`
>      - `maybe_generate_logo` (optional)
>      - `write_deploy_scripts`
> 
> 2. **In your workflow per new client:**
> 
> ```bash
> # from qi-client-template
> ./start.sh          # run spawner, create client, set profile_type, brand, maybe logo
> 
> cd /path/to/new/client
> python client_agent.py validate
> python client_agent.py organize --dry
> python client_agent.py organize
> python client_agent.py build_index
> python client_agent.py report
> ```
> 
> Open `portal/index.html` → Mini Gina + RAG search, in the client’s colors, with their logo if you gave/provided/generated one.
> 
> You’re pushing up against the edge of “too much automation,” but the way we’ve done it, everything is:
> 
> - Flat  
> - Portable  
> - Transparent  
> - And you can **skip pieces** (logo API, git push, deployment scripts) just by not configuring them.

### User
> so this template is ready with everything you sure. or what we still need to finish, do we need anything from gemini, copilot, grok, sora?

### Assistant
> Short answer:  
> **No, it’s not “ready-ready” yet.**  
> You’ve got a **solid blueprint + key code chunks**, but you still need to wire them together in the template repo and test on a real client. And **no**, you don’t *need* Gemini/Copilot/Grok/Sora for this system to work.
> 
> Let’s be precise.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1. What *is* designed and ready in principle
> 
> These pieces are conceptually done and mostly coded in the snippets:
> 
> 1. **Folder model (flat manifest)**  
>    - Top-level: `_system`, `10_profile`, `20_engagement`, `30_ops`, `40_finance`, `50_work`, `60_kb`, `70_archive`, `kb_site`, `portal`.
>    - Shallow, portable, RAG-friendly. ✅
> 
> 2. **Client Agent (`client_agent.py`) — core behaviors**
>    - `validate` — structure, depth, large file detection. ✅  
>    - `compact` — move large files to `70_archive/large_assets` + leave pointer files. ✅  
>    - `report` — HTML health report into `70_archive/reports`. ✅  
>    - `build_index` — RAG index into `portal/data/docs_index.json` from `60_kb/kb_vault` + `50_work`. ✅  
>    - `organize` — pattern-rule based **auto move + rename** with `--dry` support. ✅  
>    - **Profile-aware rules** (`profile_type`: `generic | immigration | construction`) wired via `PROFILE_RULE_SETS`. ✅
> 
> 3. **Mini Gina / Portal RAG**
>    - `portal/index.html`  
>      - Search UI + Chat UI sections. ✅  
>    - `portal/js/search.js`  
>      - Keyword scoring over `docs_index.json` + results list. ✅  
>    - `portal/js/chat.js`  
>      - Mini Gina chat:
>        - Pure offline mode: uses RAG index + templated answers. ✅  
>        - Optional `LLM_ENDPOINT` if you decide to point it at a local LLM (Ollama, etc.) ✅  
> 
> 4. **Git integration (in spawner)**
>    - `ensure_git_repo()`:
>      - Detect `.git`  
>      - Optional `git init`, `git add`, `git commit`  
>      - Optional remote + push config. ✅
> 
> 5. **Branding hooks (in spawner)**
>    - Intake for `profile_type`, colors, optional logo path. ✅  
>    - Default palettes based on client code (deterministic). ✅  
>    - Brand stored in `client.meta.json` under `"brand": { primary, secondary, accent, logo_path, source }`. ✅  
>    - Function to render CSS from `.tpl` files using brand colors (`apply_brand_to_css`). ✅ (design + pseudocode)
> 
> 6. **Deployment scaffolding**
>    - Per-client `_system/scripts/deploy_kb.sh`  
>    - `_system/scripts/deploy_portal.sh`  
>    - Stubbed with comments for CF Pages / static hosting. ✅
> 
> 7. **Logo API stub (optional)**
>    - `maybe_generate_logo()` using `QI_LOGO_API_URL` if you want auto logo creation later. ✅ (design + sample code)
> 
> So structurally and logically, the “OS” for a client **exists on paper and in chunks**.
>

> 
> ## 2. What you still need to actually build in the repo
> 
> Here’s the honest checklist of what’s missing / needs wired:
> 
> ### A. Template repo structure
> 
> You need to physically create this in `qi-client-template`:
> 
> ```text
> qi-client-template/
> ├── start.sh
> ├── client_spawner.py              # needs to be assembled from the snippets
> ├── qi_client_registry.json        # can start as []
> └── templates/
>     ├── kb_site/
>     │   ├── index.html
>     │   └── css/
>     │       └── style.css.tpl      # with {{PRIMARY}}, {{SECONDARY}}, {{ACCENT}}
>     ├── portal_shell/
>     │   ├── index.html             # with search + chat sections
>     │   ├── css/
>     │   │   └── style.css.tpl
>     │   └── js/
>     │       ├── search.js
>     │       └── chat.js
>     ├── client_agent/
>     │   └── client_agent.py        # the big one we just defined
>     ├── kb_vault_seed/             # starter .md files (even 1–2 is fine)
>     └── system_templates/          # SOP/email/whatever seed docs
> ```
> 
> None of that gets auto-created by magic. You have to:
> 
> - Make the dirs.
> - Paste in the HTML/JS/CSS we wrote.
> - Paste the agent into `templates/client_agent/client_agent.py`.
> 
> ### B. Assemble `client_spawner.py` into a coherent script
> 
> We’ve given you **pieces**, not the final file:
> 
> You need to integrate:
> 
> - The **manifest** (`CLIENT_MANIFEST`)  
> - Intake flow for:
>   - `client_name`
>   - `client_code`
>   - `profile_type` (`generic/immigration/construction`)
>   - brand colors (or auto palette)
>   - optional logo path
> - QID generator
> - Registry update (`qi_client_registry.json`)
> - Template copy mappings:
> 
>   ```python
>   TEMPLATE_MAPPINGS = {
>       "kb_site": "kb_site",
>       "portal_shell": "portal",
>       "system_templates": "_system/templates",
>       "kb_vault_seed": "60_kb/kb_vault",
>       "client_agent": ".",  # to drop client_agent.py in root
>   }
>   ```
> 
> - `apply_brand_to_css(client_root, meta)`
> - `maybe_generate_logo` (optional)
> - `write_deploy_scripts(client_root, meta)`
> - `ensure_git_repo(client_root)`
> 
> Plus the actual CLI loop:
> 
> - “New client” vs “Cleanup existing”
> - For cleanup: point at an existing client folder and maybe run:
>   - `client_agent.py validate`
>   - `client_agent.py organize --dry`
>   - etc.
> 
> Right now, **you don’t have one single `client_spawner.py`** file with all of that wired. You have the components.
> 
> ### C. Registry behavior
> 
> `qi_client_registry.json` needs:
> 
> - A **schema** like:
> 
>   ```json
>   [
>     {
>       "qid": "QCL-20251206-ABCD",
>       "client_name": "Built By Rays Construction",
>       "client_code": "c.bbr",
>       "profile_type": "construction",
>       "root_path": "/absolute/path/to/client/root",
>       "status": "active",
>       "created_at_utc": "2025-12-06T01:23:45Z"
>     }
>   ]
>   ```
> 
> - `client_spawner.py` must:
>   - Load it (or default to `[]`)
>   - Append new entry
>   - Write it back
> - If you want a “view registry” mode, add a menu option and a simple print.
> 
> ### D. CSS templates
> 
> You must actually put **placeholder tokens** in `style.css.tpl`, e.g.:
> 
> ```css
> :root {
>   --primary: {{PRIMARY}};
>   --secondary: {{SECONDARY}};
>   --accent: {{ACCENT}};
> }
> body {
>   font-family: system-ui, -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, sans-serif;
>   background-color: #f8f9fa;
>   color: #111;
> }
> a {
>   color: var(--primary);
> }
> ```
> 
> Otherwise `apply_brand_to_css` has nothing to replace.
> 
> ### E. Optional stuff you haven’t implemented at all (but is fine to skip)
> 
> - Real **logo API** (you don’t have that service yet; we just gave a stub).  
> - Real **LLM endpoint** for Mini Gina (your portal will fall back to template RAG answers if `LLM_ENDPOINT = null` — totally fine).  
> - Actual **Cloudflare deploy** commands in the `deploy_*.sh` scripts (they’re placeholders; you fill in your project names later).
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Do you need Gemini / Copilot / Grok / Sora for this?
> 
> For **this template system itself** — the spawner, the agent, the portal:
> 
> > **No. None of them are required.**
> 
> This whole stack is intentionally:
> 
> - Python + JSON  
> - HTML + CSS + vanilla JS  
> - Local git (optional remote)  
> - Optional local LLM (but not required)
> 
> Where those tools *can* help, if you want:
> 
> - **Gemini / Copilot / Grok**
>   - Helping you actually write/clean up the remaining code if you’re in an IDE.
>   - Drafting KB articles, SOPs, and docs you’ll drop into `60_kb`.
>   - Refactoring this into multiple modules later if it grows.
> 
> - **Sora**
>   - Totally unrelated to the OS itself.  
>   - Use it for client marketing videos, onboarding explainers, case-study visuals; stored under `60_kb/media` or used on their marketing site.
> 
> But for the **core template + client OS**, these are *nice-to-have content assistants*, not dependencies.
>

> > **Prompt for Cursor:**

> > 
> > - It should be an interactive CLI script with two main modes:
> >   1. **New client**  
> >   2. **Cleanup existing client**
> > 
> > ### New client flow
> > 1. Ask for:
> >    - `client_name` (e.g., “Built By Rays Construction”)  
> >    - `client_code` (e.g., `c.bbr`)  
> >    - `profile_type` (one of: `generic`, `immigration`, `construction`)
> > 2. Generate a QID like `QCL-YYYYMMDD-xxxx` where `xxxx` is a short random or hash-based code.
> > 3. Ask for the **target path** where the new client folder should be created.
> >    - Create the folder at `<target_path>/<client_code>` if it doesn’t exist.
> > 4. Create the folder structure using a `CLIENT_MANIFEST` that includes the flat layout:
> >    - `_system`, `10_profile`, `20_engagement`, `30_ops`, `40_finance`, `50_work`, `60_kb`, `70_archive`, `kb_site`, `portal` and the shallow subfolders we discussed.

> >    ```python
> >    TEMPLATE_MAPPINGS = {
> >        "kb_site": "kb_site",
> >        "portal_shell": "portal",
> >        "system_templates": "_system/templates",
> >        "kb_vault_seed": "60_kb/kb_vault",
> >        "client_agent": ".",  # drops client_agent.py at client root
> >    }
> >    ```
> > 6. Ask whether to use custom brand colors:
> >    - If yes: prompt for `primary`, `secondary`, `accent` hex codes (with sensible defaults).
> >    - If no: generate a default palette based on a deterministic hash of `client_code`.
> > 7. Ask for an optional path to a logo file for the client:
> >    - If provided, copy it to `60_kb/media/logo.ext` and store the relative path.
> >    - If not provided, optionally call a `maybe_generate_logo()` function that uses an environment variable `QI_LOGO_API_URL` to request a generated logo. If that fails, leave `logo_path` empty.
> > 8. Write `client.meta.json` in the client root with:
> >    ```json

> >      "client_code": "c.bbr",

> >      "profile_type": "construction",

> >        "secondary": "#xxxxxx",
> >        "accent": "#xxxxxx",

> >        "source": "provided" | "generated" | "default"
> >      }
> >    }
> >    ```
> > 9. Call helper functions:
> >    - `apply_brand_to_css(client_root, meta)` to render `style.css` from `style.css.tpl` in both `kb_site/css/` and `portal/css/`.
> >    - `write_deploy_scripts(client_root, meta)` to create `_system/scripts/deploy_kb.sh` and `_system/scripts/deploy_portal.sh`.
> >    - `ensure_git_repo(client_root)` to initialize a git repo and optionally set up a remote and initial push.
> > 10. Update a `qi_client_registry.json` file at the template repo root by appending an entry:
> >    ```json
> >    {
> >      "qid": "...",
> >      "client_name": "...",
> >      "client_code": "c.bbr",
> >      "profile_type": "construction",
> >      "root_path": "/absolute/path/to/client/root",
> >      "status": "active",
> >      "created_at_utc": "YYYY-MM-DDTHH:MM:SSZ"
> >    }
> >    ```
> >

> > - Confirm that `client_agent.py` exists there.
> > - Optionally offer to run:
> >   - `python client_agent.py validate`
> >   - `python client_agent.py organize --dry`
> >   - `python client_agent.py organize`
> >   - `python client_agent.py build_index`
> >   - `python client_agent.py report`
> >

> > - Use `pathlib.Path` everywhere.
> > - Keep everything in a single file, cleanly structured into helper functions.
> > - Avoid overwriting existing files unless it’s safe (e.g., rendering CSS from templates).
> > - Add clear console logging for each step.
>

> ## 2. What Gemini / Copilot / Grok should do (content + polish)

> ### 2.1. Seed KB content per profile
> 
> You want good default `kb_vault_seed/` docs for different `profile_type`s.
> 
> > **Prompt for Gemini/Copilot/Grok:**  
> > I’m building a reusable client knowledge base template for my consulting clients.  
> > I have three profile types: `generic`, `immigration`, and `construction`.
> > 
> > For each profile type, generate 5–8 concise, practical markdown files that would live in a `/60_kb/kb_vault` folder.  
> > 
> > Requirements:
> > - Neutral, professional tone – no fluff.
> > - Each file should:
> >   - Start with a `#` heading.
> >   - Be 300–700 words.
> >   - Be evergreen (not date-dependent).
> > - Topics to cover:
> >   - **generic:** onboarding, expectations, how to share files, meeting norms, how to request support, change requests, FAQ.
> >   - **immigration:** how we organize your immigration documents, what evidence categories mean, how to send updates, how to interpret USCIS notices.
> >   - **construction:** how we handle project estimates, change orders, photo documentation expectations, payment milestones, service areas, warranties.
> > 
> > Output:
> > - A directory-style listing with suggested filenames (e.g., `01_onboarding_overview.md`) and the full markdown content for each file.
> 
> You then drop those into `kb_vault_seed/` variants or just keep per-client.
>

> > - A “monthly summary” client email (`monthly_summary_email_template.md`)  
> > - A “requesting missing documents” email (`missing_docs_email_template.md`)  
> > 
> > Requirements:
> > - Use clear headings.
> > - Leave `{{placeholders}}` where I should customize.
> > - Assume I’m a systems/ops consultant acting as a strategic partner, not a generic freelancer.
> 
> Then save those under `templates/system_templates/`.

> > :root {
> >   --primary: {{PRIMARY}};
> >   --secondary: {{SECONDARY}};
> >   --accent: {{ACCENT}};
> > }
> > ```
> >

> 
> Visual beats:
